title="Christiaan Huygens">Huygens</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Newton</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Kepler</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jeremiah_Horrocks" title="Jeremiah Horrocks">Horrocks</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edmond_Halley" title="Edmond Halley">Halley</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Leonhard_Euler" title="Leonhard Euler">Euler</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jean_le_Rond_d%27Alembert" title="Jean le Rond d\'Alembert">d\'Alembert</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alexis_Clairaut" title="Alexis Clairaut">Clairaut</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph-Louis_Lagrange" title="Joseph-Louis Lagrange">Lagrange</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pierre-Simon_Laplace" title="Pierre-Simon Laplace">Laplace</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/William_Rowan_Hamilton" title="William Rowan Hamilton">Hamilton</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%A9on_Denis_Poisson" title="Sim&#233;on Denis Bernoulli</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Augustin-Louis_Cauchy" title="Augustin-Louis Cauchy">Cauchy</a></li></ul>\n</div></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;padding-top:0.15em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Classical_mechanics" title="Template:Classical mechanics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Classical_mechanics" title="Template talk:Classical mechanics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Classical_mechanics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>A <b>centripetal force</b> (from <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>centrum</i>, "center" and <i>petere</i>, "to seek"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>) is a <a href="/wiki/Force" title="Force">force</a> that makes a body follow a curved path. Its direction is always <a href="/wiki/Orthogonality" title="Orthogonality">orthogonal</a> to the motion of the body and towards the fixed point of the instantaneous <a href="/wiki/Osculating_circle" title="Osculating circle">center of curvature</a> of the path. <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a> described it as "a force by which bodies are drawn or impelled, or in any way tend, towards a point as to a centre".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> In Newtonian mechanics, gravity provides the centripetal force responsible for astronomical orbits.\n</p><p>One common example involving centripetal force is the case in which a body moves with uniform speed along a circular path. The centripetal force is directed at right angles to the motion and also along the radius towards the centre of the circular path.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hibbeler_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hibbeler-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tipler0_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tipler0-4">[4]</a></sup> The mathematical description was derived in 1659 by the Dutch physicist <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Huygens" title="Christiaan Huygens">Christiaan Huygens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toclevel-4 tocsection-12"><a href="#Alternative_approach"><span class="tocnumber">3.4.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Alternative approach</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-13"><a href="#Example:_circular_motion"><span class="tocnumber">3.4.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Example: circular motion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Notes_and_references"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Notes and references</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Formula">Formula</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Formula">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<dl><dd><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Velocity-acceleration.PNG"><img alt="Velocity-acceleration.PNG" data-file-height="513" data-file-width="695" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Velocity-acceleration.PNG/200px-Velocity-acceleration.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Velocity-acceleration.PNG/300px-Velocity-acceleration.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Velocity-acceleration.PNG/400px-Velocity-acceleration.PNG 2x" width="200"/></a></dd></dl>\n<p>The magnitude of the centripetal force on an object of mass <i>m</i> moving at <a href="/wiki/Speed#Tangential_speed" title="Speed">tangential speed</a> <i>v</i> along a path with <a href="/wiki/Radius_of_curvature" title="Radius of curvature">radius of curvature</a> <i>r</i> is:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle F=ma_{c}={\\frac {mv^{2}}{r}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>F</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle F=ma_{c}={\\frac {mv^{2}}{r}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="F = ma_c = \\frac{m v^2}{r}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/06bf957470c09aed5b2e195859a01722b0f0b7f1" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:17.21ex; height:5.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle a_{c}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle a_{c}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="a_c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81c3b8855d2273be442a8cdddc9943fd2af67bab" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.174ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centripetal_acceleration" title="Centripetal acceleration">centripetal acceleration</a>.\nThe direction of the force is toward the center of the circle in which the object is moving, or the <a href="/wiki/Osculating_circle" title="Osculating circle">osculating circle</a> (the circle that best fits the local path of the object, if the path is not circular).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>\nThe speed in the formula is squared, so twice the speed needs four times the force. The inverse relationship with the radius of curvature shows that half the radial distance requires twice the force. This force is also sometimes written in terms of the <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">angular velocity</a> <i>&#969;</i> of the object about the center of the circle, related to the tangential velocity by the formula\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v=\\omega r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v=\\omega r}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v = \\omega r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b5edc54db08559dc3e33cb3cc568126e12b46521" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.721ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>so that\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle F=mr\\omega ^{2}\\,.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>F</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle F=mr\\omega ^{2}\\,.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="F = m r \\omega^2 \\,." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f6e77093514359f3ee212abd9b6faf3d9649c6b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:11.462ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Expressed using the <a href="/wiki/Orbital_period" title="Orbital period">orbital period</a> <i>T</i> for one revolution of the circle,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\omega ={\\frac {2\\pi }{T}}\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#960;<!-- &#960; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>T</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\omega ={\\frac {2\\pi }{T}}\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\omega ={\\frac {2\\pi }{T}}\\,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e463711972f03d38362b2a4f330ed8a9d4b172b9" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:8.262ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>the equation becomes\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle F=mr\\left({\\frac {2\\pi }{T}}\\right)^{2}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>F</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<msup>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#960;<!-- &#960; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>T</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle F=mr\\left({\\frac {2\\pi }{T}}\\right)^{2}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle F=mr\\left({\\frac {2\\pi }{T}}\\right)^{2}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81a6ffd38f98d0ccc8e6f32aba249139e4529fe7" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:16.381ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p>In particle accelerators, velocity can be very high (close to the speed of light in vacuum) so the same rest mass now exerts greater inertia (relativistic mass) thereby requiring greater force for the same centripetal acceleration, so the equation becomes:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle F={\\frac {\\gamma mv^{2}}{r}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>F</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle F={\\frac {\\gamma mv^{2}}{r}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="F = \\frac{\\gamma m v^2}{r}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/33aac41322f2ccf3c1614bd907f3134a042482bc" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:11.16ex; height:5.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\gamma ={\\frac {1}{\\sqrt {1-v^{2}/c^{2}}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<msqrt>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\gamma ={\\frac {1}{\\sqrt {1-v^{2}/c^{2}}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\gamma = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{1-v^2/c^2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8b130ec5e5e9586833b7888f7cbe2433f1e295e3" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:16.929ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>is called the <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_factor" title="Lorentz factor">Lorentz factor</a>.\n</p><p>More intuitively:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle F=\\gamma mv\\omega }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>F</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle F=\\gamma mv\\omega }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle F=\\gamma mv\\omega }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4e81e2ce49b32bfe2e79df63d2202361387f29b3" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.715ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>which is the rate of change of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relativistic_momentum" title="Relativistic momentum">relativistic momentum</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\gamma mv}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\gamma mv}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\gamma mv}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5296be0d6efbb223f5a2fbef8e674a5228fcaaf4" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.43ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>)\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources">Sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Centripetal_force_diagram.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="596" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Centripetal_force_diagram.svg/220px-Centripetal_force_diagram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Centripetal_force_diagram.svg/330px-Centripetal_force_diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Centripetal_force_diagram.svg/440px-Centripetal_force_diagram.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Centripetal_force_diagram.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A body experiencing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uniform_circular_motion" title="Uniform circular motion">uniform circular motion</a> requires a centripetal force, towards the axis as shown, to maintain its circular path.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the case of an object that is swinging around on the end of a rope in a horizontal plane, the centripetal force on the object is supplied by the tension of the rope. The rope example is an example involving a \'pull\' force. The centripetal force can also be supplied as a \'push\' force, such as in the case where the normal reaction of a wall supplies the centripetal force for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wall_of_death_(motorcycle_act)" title="Wall of death (motorcycle act)">wall of death</a> rider.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Newton</a>\'s idea of a centripetal force corresponds to what is nowadays referred to as a <a href="/wiki/Central_force" title="Central force">central force</a>. When a <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">orbit</a> around a <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a>, gravity is considered to be a centripetal force even though in the case of eccentric orbits, the gravitational force is directed towards the focus, and not towards the instantaneous center of curvature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another example of centripetal force arises in the helix that is traced out when a charged particle moves in a uniform <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">magnetic field</a> in the absence of other external forces. In this case, the magnetic force is the centripetal force that acts towards the helix axis.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_of_several_cases">Analysis of several cases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Analysis of several cases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Below are three examples of increasing complexity, with derivations of the formulas governing velocity and acceleration.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniform_circular_motion">Uniform circular motion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Uniform circular motion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uniform_circular_motion" title="Uniform circular motion">Uniform circular motion</a></div>\n<p>Uniform circular motion refers to the case of constant rate of rotation. Here are two approaches to describing this case.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Calculus_derivation">Calculus derivation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Calculus derivation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In two dimensions, the position vector <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {r}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">r</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {r}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\textbf{r}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8a907369fc0aa51241fcd0620f96478563a6c810" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.102ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>, which has magnitude (length) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> and directed at an angle <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\theta }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\theta }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\theta " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e5ab2664b422d53eb0c7df3b87e1360d75ad9af" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> above the x-axis, can be expressed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinates" title="Cartesian coordinates">Cartesian coordinates</a> using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unit_vectors" title="Unit vectors">unit vectors</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\hat {x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\hat {x}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\hat {x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/18d95a7845e4e16ffb7e18ab37a208d0ab18e0e0" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\hat {y}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>y</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\hat {y}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\hat {y}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3dc8de3d8ea01304329ef9518fad7a6d196c4c01" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.302ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {r}}=r\\cos(\\theta ){\\hat {x}}+r\\sin(\\theta ){\\hat {y}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">r</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b34bc4118bcd664ef235f4c0025e40aff75d601f" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:24.957ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>Assume <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uniform_circular_motion" title="Uniform circular motion">uniform circular motion</a>, which requires three things.\n</p>\n<ol><li>The object moves only on a circle.</li>\n<li>The radius of the circle <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> does not change in time.</li>\n<li>The object moves with constant <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">angular velocity</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\omega }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\omega }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\omega " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/48eff443f9de7a985bb94ca3bde20813ea737be8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.446ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> around the circle. Therefore, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\theta =\\omega t}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; width:6.474ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle t}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle t}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="t" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/65658b7b223af9e1acc877d848888ecdb4466560" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.84ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is time.</li></ol>\n<p>Now find the <a href="/wiki/Velocity" title="Velocity">velocity</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {v}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">v</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {v}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\textbf{v}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ea31d06d1f25599e56d852db92f3ebc85ac75a8d" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.411ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> and <a href="/wiki/Acceleration" title="Acceleration">acceleration</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">a</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {a}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\textbf{a}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af9f1604cec45bc8d60e31610f9ec1b7c6599b68" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.299ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> of the motion by taking derivatives of position with respect to time.\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd><dl><dd><dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {r}}=r\\cos(\\omega t){\\hat {x}}+r\\sin(\\omega t){\\hat {y}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">r</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>y</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\ddot {\\textbf {r}}}={\\textbf {a}}=-r\\omega ^{2}\\cos(\\omega t){\\hat {x}}-r\\omega ^{2}\\sin(\\omega t){\\hat {y}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" \\ddot{\\textbf{r}} = \\textbf{a} = - r \\omega^2 \\cos(\\omega t) \\hat{x} - r \\omega^2 \\sin(\\omega t) \\hat{y} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d609870d2dccf227c1d4fe2e263456c45467be5b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:37.967ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {a}}=-\\omega ^{2}(r\\cos(\\omega t){\\hat {x}}+r\\sin(\\omega t){\\hat {y}})}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">a</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mi>sin</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>y</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {a}}=-\\omega ^{2}(r\\cos(\\omega t){\\hat {x}}+r\\sin(\\omega t){\\hat {y}})}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" \\textbf{a} = - \\omega^2 (r \\cos(\\omega t) \\hat{x} + r \\sin(\\omega t) \\hat{y}) " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4a1e29adf209a9612574ed4131d725ed4d576540" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:33.015ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>Notice that the term in parenthesis is the original expression of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {r}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">r</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {r}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\textbf{r}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8a907369fc0aa51241fcd0620f96478563a6c810" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.102ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinates" title="Cartesian coordinates">Cartesian coordinates</a>. Consequently,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {a}}=-\\omega ^{2}{\\textbf {r}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">a</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext mathvariant="bold">r</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\textbf {a}}=-\\omega ^{2}{\\textbf {r}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" \\textbf{a} = - \\omega^2 \\textbf{r}. " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/741274c060a908cfd95284007943293cc09370bd" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:10.455ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>negative shows that the acceleration is pointed towards the center of the circle (opposite the radius), hence it is called "centripetal" (i.e. "center-seeking"). While objects naturally follow a straight path (due to <a href="/wiki/Inertia" title="Inertia">inertia</a>), this centripetal acceleration describes the circular motion path caused by a centripetal force.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Derivation_using_vectors">Derivation using vectors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Derivation using vectors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. The rotation itself is represented by the angular velocity vector <b>&#937;</b>, which is normal to the plane of the orbit (using the <a href="/wiki/Right-hand_rule" title="Right-hand rule">right-hand rule</a>) and has magnitude given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle |\\mathbf {\\Omega } |={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} t}}=\\omega \\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle |\\mathbf {\\Omega } |={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} t}}=\\omega \\ ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" |\\mathbf{\\Omega}| = \\frac {\\mathrm{d} \\theta } {\\mathrm{d}t} = \\omega \\ , " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a0f2f065452864d2f700d78aa215398852221bb9" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:15.314ex; height:5.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>with <i>&#952;</i> the angular position at time <i>t</i>. In this subsection, d<i>&#952;</i>/d<i>t</i> is assumed constant, independent of time. The distance traveled <b>d&#8467;</b> of the particle in time d<i>t</i> along the circular path is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathrm {d} {\\boldsymbol {\\ell }}=\\mathbf {\\Omega } \\times \\mathbf {r} (t)\\mathrm {d} t\\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold-italic">&#8467;<!-- &#8467; width:17.375ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>which, by properties of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vector_cross_product" title="Vector cross product">vector cross product</a>, has magnitude <i>r</i>d<i>&#952;</i> and is in the direction tangent to the circular path.\n</p><p>Consequently,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {r} }{\\mathrm {d} t}}=\\lim _{{\\Delta }t\\to 0}{\\frac {\\mathbf {r} (t+{\\Delta }t)-\\mathbf {r} (t)}{{\\Delta }t}}={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} {\\boldsymbol {\\ell }}}{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<munder>\n<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">lim</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; width:35.495ex; height:6.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>In other words,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {v} \\ {\\stackrel {\\mathrm {def} }{=}}\\ {\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {r} }{\\mathrm {d} t}}={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {\\boldsymbol {\\ell }} }{\\mathrm {d} t}}=\\mathbf {\\Omega } \\times \\mathbf {r} (t)\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-REL">\n<mover>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OP MJX-fixedlimits">\n<mo>=</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">f</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold-italic">&#8467;<!-- &#8467; width:41.307ex; height:5.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Triple_product#Vector_triple_product" title="Triple product">Lagrange\'s formula</a> states:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {a} \\times \\left(\\mathbf {b} \\times \\mathbf {c} \\right)=\\mathbf {b} \\left(\\mathbf {a} \\cdot \\mathbf {c} \\right)-\\mathbf {c} \\left(\\mathbf {a} \\cdot \\mathbf {b} \\right)\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">a</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#215;<!-- &#215; width:34.713ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Applying Lagrange\'s formula with the observation that <b>&#937; &#8226; r</b>(<i>t</i>) = 0 at all times,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {a} =-{|\\mathbf {\\Omega |} }^{2}\\mathbf {r} (t)\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">a</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo mathvariant="bold" stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {a} =-{|\\mathbf {\\Omega |} }^{2}\\mathbf {r} (t)\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" \\mathbf{a} = - {|\\mathbf{\\Omega|}}^2 \\mathbf{r}(t) \\ ." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1fe0a21658fde14fe1ca11a3a356d74e405c8a84" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.559ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>In words, the acceleration is pointing directly opposite to the radial displacement <b>r</b> at all times, and has a magnitude:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle |\\mathbf {a} |=|\\mathbf {r} (t)|\\left({\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\right)^{2}=r{\\omega }^{2}\\ }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">a</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle |\\mathbf {a} |=|\\mathbf {r} (t)|\\left({\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\right)^{2}=r{\\omega }^{2}\\ }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" |\\mathbf{a}| = |\\mathbf{r}(t)| \\left ( \\frac {\\mathrm{d} \\theta}{\\mathrm{d}t} \\right) ^2 = r {\\omega}^2\\ " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3fc08d46f072b0d2c7e71a2829072d32b9ce7752" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:25.659ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>where vertical bars |...| denote the vector magnitude, which in the case of <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>) is simply the radius <i>r</i> of the path. This result agrees with the previous section, though the notation is slightly different.\n</p><p>When the rate of rotation is made constant in the analysis of <a href="/wiki/Centripetal_force#Nonuniform_circular_motion" title="Centripetal force">nonuniform circular motion</a>, that analysis agrees with this one.\n</p><p>A merit of the vector approach is that it is manifestly independent of any coordinate system.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Example:_The_banked_turn">Example: The banked turn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Example: The banked turn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Banked_turn" title="Banked turn">Banked turn</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Reactive_centrifugal_force" title="Reactive centrifugal force">Reactive centrifugal force</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banked_turn.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="805" data-file-width="660" decoding="async" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Banked_turn.svg/220px-Banked_turn.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Banked_turn.svg/330px-Banked_turn.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Banked_turn.svg/440px-Banked_turn.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banked_turn.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Upper panel: Ball on a banked circular track moving with constant speed <i>v</i>; Lower panel: Forces on the ball</div></div></div>\n<p>The upper panel in the image at right shows a ball in circular motion on a banked curve. The curve is banked at an angle <i>&#952;</i> from the horizontal, and the surface of the road is considered to be slippery. The objective is to find what angle the bank must have so the ball does not slide off the road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lerner_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lerner-11">[11]</a></sup> Intuition tells us that, on a flat curve with no banking at all, the ball will simply slide off the road; while with a very steep banking, the ball will slide to the center unless it travels the curve rapidly.\n</p><p>Apart from any acceleration that might occur in the direction of the path, the lower panel of the image above indicates the forces on the ball. There are <i>two</i> forces; one is the force of gravity vertically downward through the center of mass of the ball <i>m</i><b>g</b>, where <i>m</i> is the mass of the ball and <b>g</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_acceleration" title="Gravitational acceleration">gravitational acceleration</a>; the second is the upward <a href="/wiki/Normal_force" title="Normal force">normal force</a> exerted by the road at a right angle to the road surface <i>m</i><b>a</b><sub>n</sub>. The centripetal force demanded by the curved motion is also shown above. This centripetal force is not a third force applied to the ball, but rather must be provided by the <a href="/wiki/Net_force" title="Net force">net force</a> on the ball resulting from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vector_addition" title="Vector addition">vector addition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Normal_force" title="Normal force">normal force</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Force_of_gravity" title="Force of gravity">force of gravity</a>. The resultant or <a href="/wiki/Net_force" title="Net force">net force</a> on the ball found by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vector_addition" title="Vector addition">vector addition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Normal_force" title="Normal force">normal force</a> exerted by the road and vertical force due to <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">gravity</a> must equal the centripetal force dictated by the need to travel a circular path. The curved motion is maintained so long as this net force provides the centripetal force requisite to the motion.\n</p><p>The horizontal net force on the ball is the horizontal component of the force from the road, which has magnitude |<b>F</b><sub>h</sub>| = <i>m</i>|<b>a</b><sub>n</sub>|sin<i>&#952;</i>. The vertical component of the force from the road must counteract the gravitational force: |<b>F</b><sub>v</sub>| = <i>m</i>|<b>a</b><sub>n</sub>|cos<i>&#952;</i> = <i>m</i>|<b>g</b>|, which implies |<b>a</b><sub>n</sub>|=|<b>g</b>| / cos<i>&#952;</i>. Substituting into the above formula for |<b>F</b><sub>h</sub>| yields a horizontal force to be:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle |\\mathbf {F} _{\\mathrm {h} }|=m|\\mathbf {g} |{\\frac {\\mathrm {sin} \\ \\theta }{\\mathrm {cos} \\ \\theta }}=m|\\mathbf {g} |\\mathrm {tan} \\ \\theta \\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">F</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">h</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">g</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">o</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">g</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle |\\mathbf {F} _{\\mathrm {h} }|=m|\\mathbf {g} |{\\frac {\\mathrm {sin} \\ \\theta }{\\mathrm {cos} \\ \\theta }}=m|\\mathbf {g} |\\mathrm {tan} \\ \\theta \\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" |\\mathbf{F}_\\mathrm{h}| = m |\\mathbf{g}| \\frac { \\mathrm{sin}\\ \\theta}{ \\mathrm {cos}\\ \\theta} = m|\\mathbf{g}| \\mathrm{tan}\\ \\theta \\ . " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f6f729a660dcc4e5947c42112db6541d451c6cd0" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:31.538ex; height:5.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>On the other hand, at velocity |<b>v</b>| on a circular path of radius <i>r</i>, kinematics says that the force needed to turn the ball continuously into the turn is the radially inward centripetal force <b>F</b><sub>c</sub> of magnitude:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline alt="|\\mathbf{F}_\\mathrm{c}| = m |\\mathbf{a}_\\mathrm{c}| = \\frac{m|\\mathbf{v}|^2}{r} \\ . " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d2723fb42d5dc62af57d1f5d5a994c7a5466a305" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:23.594ex; height:6.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Consequently, the ball is in a stable path when the angle of the road is set to satisfy the condition:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle m|\\mathbf {g} |\\mathrm {tan} \\ \\theta ={\\frac {m|\\mathbf {v} |^{2}}{r}}\\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">g</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle m|\\mathbf {g} |\\mathrm {tan} \\ \\theta ={\\frac {m|\\mathbf {v} |^{2}}{r}}\\ ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="m |\\mathbf{g}| \\mathrm{tan}\\ \\theta = \\frac{m|\\mathbf{v}|^2}{r} \\ ," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2f49bb73602503361085d2466169cdff0ddb5381" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:20.663ex; height:6.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>or,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathrm {tan} \\ \\theta ={\\frac {|\\mathbf {v} |^{2}}{|\\mathbf {g} |r}}\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">g</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathrm {tan} \\ \\theta ={\\frac {|\\mathbf {v} |^{2}}{|\\mathbf {g} |r}}\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" \\mathrm{tan}\\ \\theta = \\frac {|\\mathbf{v}|^2} {|\\mathbf{g}|r} \\ ." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bc74a45beb50c8d0cc4dc3285e98624ccce96d9e" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:13.952ex; height:6.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>As the angle of bank <i>&#952;</i> approaches 90&#176;, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangent_function" title="Tangent function">tangent function</a> approaches infinity, allowing larger values for |<b>v</b>|<sup>2</sup>/<i>r</i>. In words, this equation states that for greater speeds (bigger |<b>v</b>|) the road must be banked more steeply (a larger value for <i>&#952;</i>), and for sharper turns (smaller <i>r</i>) the road also must be banked more steeply, which accords with intuition. When the angle <i>&#952;</i> does not satisfy the above condition, the horizontal component of force exerted by the road does not provide the correct centripetal force, and an additional frictional force tangential to the road surface is called upon to provide the difference. If <a href="/wiki/Friction" title="Friction">friction</a> cannot do this (that is, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_friction" title="Coefficient of friction">coefficient of friction</a> is exceeded), the ball slides to a different radius where the balance can be realized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schaum_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schaum-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Darbyshire_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Darbyshire-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>These ideas apply to air flight as well. See the FAA pilot\'s manual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAA_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FAA-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nonuniform_circular_motion">Nonuniform circular motion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Nonuniform circular motion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Circular_motion" title="Circular motion">Circular motion</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-uniform_circular_motion" title="Non-uniform circular motion">Non-uniform circular motion</a></div>\n<table The acceleration now has a tangential component, as shown the image at right. This case is used to demonstrate a derivation strategy based on a <a href="/wiki/Polar_coordinate_system" title="Polar coordinate system">polar coordinate system</a>.\n</p><p>Let <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>) be a vector that describes the position of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Point_mass" title="Point mass">point mass</a> as a function of time. Since we are assuming <a href="/wiki/Circular_motion" title="Circular motion">circular motion</a>, let <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>) = <i>R</i>&#183;<b>u</b><sub>r</sub>, where <i>R</i> is a constant (the radius of the circle) and <b>u</b><sub>r</sub> is the <a href="/wiki/Unit_vector" title="Unit vector">unit vector</a> pointing from the origin to the point mass. The direction of <b>u</b><sub>r</sub> is described by <i>&#952;</i>, the angle between the x-axis and the unit vector, measured counterclockwise from the x-axis. The other unit vector for polar coordinates, <b>u</b><sub>&#952;</sub> is perpendicular to <b>u</b><sub>r</sub> and points in the direction of increasing <i>&#952;</i>. These polar unit vectors can be expressed in terms of <a href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinate_system" title="Cartesian coordinate system">Cartesian</a> unit vectors in the <i>x</i> and <i>y</i> directions, denoted <b>i</b> and <b>j</b> respectively:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><b>u</b><sub>r</sub> = cos<i>&#952;</i> <b>i</b> + sin<i>&#952;</i> <b>j</b></dd></dl>\n<p>and\n</p>\n<dl><dd><b>u</b><sub>&#952;</sub> = -sin<i>&#952;</i> <b>i</b> + cos<i>&#952;</i> <b>j</b>.</dd></dl>\n<p>One can differentiate to find velocity:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {v} =r{\\frac {\\mathrm the velocity should be directed tangentially to the circle, and that the magnitude of the velocity should be <i>r&#969;</i>. height:5.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where |<b>v</b>| = <i>r</i> &#969; is the magnitude of the velocity (the speed).\n</p><p>These equations express mathematically that, in the case of an object that moves along a circular path with a changing speed, the acceleration of the body may be decomposed into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perpendicular_component" title="Perpendicular component">perpendicular component</a> that changes the direction of motion (the centripetal acceleration), and a parallel, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangential_component" title="Tangential component">tangential component</a>, that changes the speed.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_planar_motion">General planar motion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: General planar Their rotation in time <i>dt</i> is <i>d</i>&#952;, just the same angle as the rotation of the trajectory <b>r</b> ( <i>t</i> ).</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Polar_coordinates">Polar coordinates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Polar coordinates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Centripetal+force%22" rel="nofollow">"Centripetal force"</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Centripetal+force%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">news</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Centripetal+force%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Centripetal+force%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Centripetal+force%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Centripetal+force%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2009</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The above results can be derived perhaps more simply in <a href="/wiki/Polar_coordinate_system" title="Polar coordinate system">polar coordinates</a>, and at the same time extended to general motion within a plane, as shown next. Polar coordinates in the plane employ a radial unit vector <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> and an angular unit vector <b>u</b><sub>&#952;</sub>, as shown above.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polar_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-polar-16">[16]</a></sup> A particle at position <b>r</b> is described by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {r} =\\rho \\mathbf {u} _{\\rho }\\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {r} =\\rho \\mathbf {u} _{\\rho }\\ ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mathbf{r} = \\rho \\mathbf{u}_{\\rho} \\ , " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4dcf99817c25534e0e6bd8f8116b332d902fa70a" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:9.197ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where the notation <i>&#961;</i> is used to describe the distance of the path from the origin instead of <i>R</i> to emphasize that this distance is not fixed, but varies with time. The unit vector <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> travels with the particle and always points in the same direction as <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>). Unit vector <b>u</b><sub>&#952;</sub> also travels with the particle and stays orthogonal to <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub>. Thus, <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> and <b>u</b><sub>&#952;</sub> form a local Cartesian coordinate system attached to the particle, and tied to the path traveled by the particle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> By moving the unit vectors so their tails coincide, as seen in the circle at the left of the image above, it is seen that <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> and <b>u</b><sub>&#952;</sub> form a right-angled pair with tips on the unit circle that trace back and forth on the perimeter of this circle with the same angle <i>&#952;</i>(<i>t</i>) as <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>).\n</p><p>When the particle moves, its velocity is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {v} ={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\rho }{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\mathbf {u} _{\\rho }+\\rho {\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {u} _{\\rho }}{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">v</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/52a934e6903f33667be9c55d6624ec499f954d6c" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:20.373ex; height:5.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>To evaluate the velocity, the derivative of the unit vector <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> is needed. Because <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> is a unit vector, its magnitude is fixed, and it can change only in direction, that is, its change d<b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> has a component only perpendicular to <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub>. When the trajectory <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>) rotates an amount d<i>&#952;</i>, <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub>, which points in the same direction as <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>), also rotates by d<i>&#952;</i>. See image above. Therefore, the change in <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {u} _{\\rho }=\\mathbf {u} _{\\theta }\\mathrm {d} \\theta \\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; As with <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub>, <b>u</b><sub>&#952;</sub> is a unit vector and can only rotate without changing size. To remain orthogonal to <b>u</b><sub>&#961;</sub> while the trajectory <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>) rotates an amount d<i>&#952;</i>, <b>u</b><sub>&#952;</sub>, which is orthogonal to <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>), also rotates by d<i>&#952;</i>. See image above.
