width:35.382ex; height:7.509ex;"/></span>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle =\\mathbf {u} _{\\rho }\\left[-{\\frac {v^{2}}{r}}\\right]+\\mathbf {u} _{\\theta }\\left[{\\frac {\\mathrm {d} v}{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\right]\\ }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mrow>\n<mo>[</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>]</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mrow>\n<mo>[</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>]</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle =\\mathbf {u} _{\\rho }\\left[-{\\frac {v^{2}}{r}}\\right]+\\mathbf {u} _{\\theta }\\left[{\\frac {\\mathrm {d} v}{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\right]\\ }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle =\\mathbf {u} _{\\rho }\\left[-{\\frac {v^{2}}{r}}\\right]+\\mathbf {u} _{\\theta }\\left[{\\frac {\\mathrm {d} v}{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\right]\\ }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/89b7dd97a15e78eb9aa16ccda4f969e2d41491fa" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:25.084ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v=v_{\\theta }.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v=v_{\\theta }.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" v = v_{\\theta}. " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/85d717e45833e0c830ca46adc991305360232362" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:7.004ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>\n</p><p>These results agree with those above for <a href="/wiki/Centripetal_force#Nonuniform_circular_motion" title="Centripetal force">nonuniform circular motion</a>. See also the article on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-uniform_circular_motion" title="Non-uniform circular motion">non-uniform circular motion</a>. If this acceleration is multiplied by the particle mass, the leading term is the centripetal force and the negative of the second term related to angular acceleration is sometimes called the <a href="/wiki/Euler_force" title="Euler force">Euler force</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lanczos_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lanczos-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>For trajectories other than circular motion, for example, the more general trajectory envisioned in the image above, the instantaneous center of rotation and radius of curvature of the trajectory are related only indirectly to the coordinate system defined by <b>u<sub>&#961;</sub></b> and <b>u<sub>&#952;</sub></b> and to the length |<b>r</b>(<i>t</i>)| = <i>&#961;</i>. Consequently, in the general case, it is not straightforward to disentangle the centripetal and Euler terms from the above general acceleration equation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis-20">[20]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lee_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lee-21">[21]</a></sup> To deal directly with this issue, local coordinates are preferable, as discussed next.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_coordinates">Local coordinates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Local coordinates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Local_unit_vectors.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="562" data-file-width="835" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Local_unit_vectors.PNG/220px-Local_unit_vectors.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Local_unit_vectors.PNG/330px-Local_unit_vectors.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Local_unit_vectors.PNG/440px-Local_unit_vectors.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Local_unit_vectors.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Local coordinate system for planar motion on a curve. Two different positions are shown for distances <i>s</i> and <i>s</i> + <i>ds</i> along the curve. At each position <i>s</i>, unit vector <b>u</b><sub>n</sub> points along the outward normal to the curve and unit vector <b>u</b><sub>t</sub> is tangential to the path. The radius of curvature of the path is &#961; as found from the rate of rotation of the tangent to the curve with respect to arc length, and is the radius of the <a href="/wiki/Osculating_circle" title="Osculating circle">osculating circle</a> at position <i>s</i>. The unit circle on the left shows the rotation of the unit vectors with <i>s</i>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Local coordinates mean a set of coordinates that travel with the particle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-observer_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-observer-22">[22]</a></sup> and have orientation determined by the path of the particle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ito_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ito-23">[23]</a></sup> Unit vectors are formed as shown in the image at right, both tangential and normal to the path. This coordinate system sometimes is referred to as <i>intrinsic</i> or <i>path coordinates</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kumar_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kumar-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rao_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rao-25">[25]</a></sup> or <i>nt-coordinates</i>, for <i>normal-tangential</i>, referring to these unit vectors. These coordinates are a very special example of a more general concept of local coordinates from the theory of differential forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morita_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morita-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Distance along the path of the particle is the arc length <i>s</i>, considered to be a known function of time.\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s=s(t)\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s=s(t)\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" s = s(t) \\ . " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bcea5a3bc0a52f17e27709828077122b5fffa3c2" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.156ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>A center of curvature is defined at each position <i>s</i> located a distance <i>&#961;</i> (the <a href="/wiki/Osculating_circle#Mathematical_description" title="Osculating circle">radius of curvature</a>) from the curve on a line along the normal <b>u</b><sub>n</sub> (<i>s</i>). The required distance <i>&#961;</i>(<i>s</i>) at arc length <i>s</i> is defined in terms of the rate of rotation of the tangent to the curve, which in turn is determined by the path itself. If the orientation of the tangent relative to some starting position is <i>&#952;</i>(<i>s</i>), then <i>&#961;</i>(<i>s</i>) is defined by the derivative d<i>&#952;</i>/d<i>s</i>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {1}{\\rho (s)}}=\\kappa (s)={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} s}}\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#954;<!-- &#954; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>s</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\frac {1}{\\rho (s)}}=\\kappa (s)={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} s}}\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\frac{1} {\\rho (s)} = \\kappa (s) = \\frac {\\mathrm{d}\\theta}{\\mathrm{d}s}\\ . " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b5c4902ca10a174327f5c1a33ed2ff61dc95cb99" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:19.82ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>The radius of curvature usually is taken as positive (that is, as an absolute value), while the <i><a href="/wiki/Curvature#Local_expressions" title="Curvature">curvature</a></i> <i>&#954;</i> is a signed quantity.\n</p><p>A geometric approach to finding the center of curvature and the radius of curvature uses a limiting process leading to the <a href="/wiki/Osculating_circle" title="Osculating circle">osculating circle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-osculating_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-osculating-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chen0_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chen0-28">[28]</a></sup> See image above.\n</p><p>Using these coordinates, the motion along the path is viewed as a succession of circular paths of ever-changing center, and at each position <i>s</i> constitutes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-uniform_circular_motion" title="Non-uniform circular motion">non-uniform circular motion</a> at that position with radius <i>&#961;</i>. The local value of the angular rate of rotation then is given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\omega (s)={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} t}}={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} s}}{\\frac {\\mathrm {d} s}{\\mathrm {d} t}}={\\frac {1}{\\rho (s)}}\\ {\\frac {\\mathrm {d} s}{\\mathrm {d} t}}={\\frac {v(s)}{\\rho (s)}}\\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#969;<!-- &#969; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\omega (s)={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} t}}={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} \\theta }{\\mathrm {d} s}}{\\frac {\\mathrm {d} s}{\\mathrm {d} t}}={\\frac {1}{\\rho (s)}}\\ {\\frac {\\mathrm {d} s}{\\mathrm {d} t}}={\\frac {v(s)}{\\rho (s)}}\\ ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" \\omega(s) = \\frac{\\mathrm{d}\\theta}{\\mathrm{d}t} = \\frac{\\mathrm{d}\\theta}{\\mathrm{d}s} \\frac {\\mathrm{d}s}{\\mathrm{d}t} = \\frac{1}{\\rho(s)}\\ \\frac {\\mathrm{d}s}{\\mathrm{d}t} = \\frac{v(s)}{\\rho(s)}\\ ," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/295650c9f5fbe7feac6a57fbfd570c4d8288f643" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:41.3ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>with the local speed <i>v</i> given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v(s)={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} s}{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>s</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v(s)={\\frac {\\mathrm {d} s}{\\mathrm {d} t}}\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" v(s) = \\frac {\\mathrm{d}s}{\\mathrm{d}t}\\ . height:5.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>As for the other examples above, because unit vectors cannot change magnitude, their rate of change is always perpendicular to their direction (see the left-hand insert in the image above):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gregory_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gregory-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {d\\mathbf {u} _{\\mathrm {n} }(s)}{ds}}=\\mathbf {u} _{\\mathrm {t} }(s){\\frac {d\\theta }{ds}}=\\mathbf {u} _{\\mathrm {t} }(s){\\frac {1}{\\rho }}\\ ;}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>d</mi>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>s</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a6dbb08ccbabac54ebc6ee7b5ff3dbaa85a16abd" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:22.701ex; height:5.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>In this local coordinate system, the acceleration resembles the expression for <a href="#Nonuniform_circular_motion">nonuniform circular motion</a> with the local radius <i>&#961;</i>(<i>s</i>), and the centripetal acceleration is identified as the second term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shelley_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shelley-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Extending this approach to three dimensional space curves leads to the <a href="/wiki/Frenet%E2%80%93Serret_formulas" title="Frenet&#8211;Serret formulas">Frenet&#8211;Serret formulas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andrews_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andrews-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chand_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chand-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_approach">Alternative approach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Alternative approach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>Looking at the image above, one might wonder whether adequate account has been taken of the difference in curvature between <i>&#961;</i>(<i>s</i>) and <i>&#961;</i>(<i>s</i> + d<i>s</i>) in computing the arc length as d<i>s</i> = <i>&#961;</i>(<i>s</i>)d<i>&#952;</i>. Reassurance on this point can be found using a more formal approach outlined below. This approach also makes connection with the article on <a href="/wiki/Curvature#Local_expressions" title="Curvature">curvature</a>.\n</p><p>To introduce the unit vectors of the local coordinate system, one approach is to begin in Cartesian coordinates and describe the local coordinates in terms of these Cartesian coordinates. In terms of arc length <i>s</i>, let the path be described as:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curvature_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-curvature-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {r} (s)=\\left[x(s),\\ y(s)\\right]\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mo>[</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>y</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>]</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {r} (s)=\\left[x(s),\\ y(s)\\right]\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mathbf{r}(s) = \\left[ x(s),\\ y(s) \\right] \\ . " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f50cd41ec8111237c20ad282b5ba391db70c932" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:19.908ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Then an incremental displacement along the path d<i>s</i> is described by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {r} (s)=\\left[\\mathrm {d} x(s),\\ \\mathrm {d} scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<msup>\n<mi>y</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>]</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathrm {d} \\mathbf {r} (s)=\\left[\\mathrm {d} x(s),\\ \\mathrm {d} y(s)\\right]=\\left[x\'(s),\\ y\'(s)\\right]\\mathrm {d} s\\ ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mathrm{d}\\mathbf{r}(s) = \\left[ \\mathrm{d}x(s),\\ \\mathrm{d}y(s) \\right] = \\left[ x\'(s),\\ y\'(s) \\right] \\mathrm{d}s \\ , " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" primes are introduced to denote derivatives with respect to <i>s</i>. The magnitude of this displacement is d<i>s</i>, showing that:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shabana_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shabana-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\left[x\'(s)^{2}+y\'(s)^{2}\\right]=1\\ .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow>\n<mo>[</mo>\n<mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>y</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mo>]</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\left[x\'(s)^{2}+y\'(s)^{2}\\right]=1\\ .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\left[ x\'(s)^2 + y\'(s)^2 \\right] = 1 \\ . " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/50c42e82eda34ce15d98149c930dfb7ba7cec77d" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:22.036ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span> <span id="Eq._1"></span>(Eq. 1)</dd></dl>\n<p>This displacement is necessarily a tangent to the curve at <i>s</i>, showing that the unit vector tangent to the curve is:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u} _{\\mathrm {t} }(s)=\\left[x\'(s),\\ y\'(s)\\right]\\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mo>[</mo>\n<mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<msup>\n<mi>y</mi>\n<mo>&#8242;</mo>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>]</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {u} _{\\mathrm {t} }(s)=\\left[x\'(s),\\ y\'(s)\\right]\\ ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mathbf{u}_\\mathrm{t}(s) = \\left[ x\'(s), \\ y\'(s) \\right] \\ , " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/145d8ad33bedd2dd0d363d83a3b28f08d9271422" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:25.652ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Orthogonality" title="Orthogonality">Orthogonality</a> can be verified by showing that the vector <a href="/wiki/Dot_product" title="Dot product">dot product</a> is zero. The unit magnitude of these vectors is a consequence of <a href="#Eq._1">Eq. 1</a>. Using the tangent vector, the angle <i>&#952;</i> of the tangent to the curve is given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sin \\theta ={\\frac {y\'(s)}{\\sqrt {x\'(s)^{2}+y\'(s)^{2}}}}=y\'(s)\\ ;}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>sin</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt=" = \\left(\\frac{\\mathrm{d}^2s}{\\mathrm{d}t^2}\\right)\\mathbf{u}_\\mathrm{t}(s) - \\left(\\frac{\\mathrm{d}s}{\\mathrm{d}t}\\right) ^2 \\frac{1}{\\rho} \\mathbf{u}_\\mathrm{n}(s) \\ , " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d9b3a9b33c6cf8486e2e4548ae38a94e130849a7" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:35.124ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>as can be verified by taking the dot product with the unit vectors <b>u</b><sub>t</sub>(<i>s</i>) and <b>u</b><sub>n</sub>(<i>s</i>). This result for acceleration is the same as that for circular motion based on the radius <i>&#961;</i>. Using this coordinate system in the inertial frame, it is easy to identify the force normal to the trajectory as the centripetal force and that parallel to the trajectory as the tangential force. From a qualitative standpoint, the path can be approximated by an arc of a circle for a limited time, and for the limited time a particular radius of curvature applies, the centrifugal and Euler forces can be analyzed on the basis of circular motion with that radius.\n</p><p>This result for acceleration agrees with that found earlier. However, in this approach, the question of the change in radius of curvature with <i>s</i> is handled completely formally, consistent with a geometric interpretation, but not relying upon it, thereby avoiding any questions the image above might suggest about neglecting the variation in <i>&#961;</i>.\n<span id="circular_motion"></span>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Example:_circular_motion">Example: circular motion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Example: circular motion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Centripetal_force&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. \\ y = \\alpha \\sin\\frac{s}{\\alpha} \\ ." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/39eaa7fcfb52c46abe01e9f7743bca42e344eed5" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:27.243ex; height:4.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Then:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle x^{2}+y^{2}=\\alpha ^{2}\\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>y</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; The position <i>s</i> = 0 corresponds to [<i>&#945;</i>, 0], or 3 o\'clock. " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/29f755d9d1bb8f6f884a3bdc8ae8d1be5147674a" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:45.408ex; height:5.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>To obtain velocity and acceleration, a time-dependence for <i>s</i> is necessary. For counterclockwise motion at variable speed <i>v</i>(<i>t</i>):\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s(t)=\\int _{0}^{t}\\ dt^{\\prime }\\ v(t^{\\prime })\\ ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msubsup>\n<mo>&#8747;<!-- &#8747; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>d</mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi class="MJX-variant" mathvariant="normal">&#8242;<!-- &#8242; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi class="MJX-variant" mathvariant="normal">&#8242;<!-- &#8242; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s(t)=\\int _{0}^{t}\\ dt^{\\prime }\\ v(t^{\\prime })\\ ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="s(t) = \\int_0^t \\ dt^{\\prime} \\ v(t^{\\prime}) \\ , " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0c0792f3dd6b60d2b5e4ce98e467196a60f3bc28" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:20.105ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <i>v</i>(<i>t</i>) is the speed and <i>t</i> is time, and <i>s</i>(<i>t</i> = 0) = 0. Then:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {v} =v(t)\\mathbf {u} already is established that &#945; = &#961;. The description of the particle motion remains a description from the stationary observer\'s point of view.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Notice that this local coordinate system is not autonomous; for example, its rotation in time is dictated by the trajectory traced by the particle. Butterworth-Heinemann. p.&#160;5. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7506-6169-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7506-6169-0">978-0-7506-6169-0</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Orbital+Mechanics+for+Engineering+Students&amp;rft.pages=5&amp;rft.pub=Butterworth-Heinemann&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-7506-6169-0&amp;rft.au=Howard+D.+Curtis&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACentripetal+force"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Lee-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Lee_21-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">S. Hackensack NJ: World Scientific. p.&#160;37. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-981-256-182-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-981-256-182-4">978-981-256-182-4</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Accelerator+physics&amp;rft.place=Hackensack+NJ&amp;rft.pages=37&amp;rft.edition=2nd&amp;rft.pub=World+Scientific&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-981-256-182-4&amp;rft.au=S.+Y.+Lee&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3DVTc8Sdld5S8C%26pg%3DPA37%26dq%3Dorbit%2B%2522coordinate%2Bsystem%2522&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACentripetal+force"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-observer-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-observer_22-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <i>observer</i> of the motion along the curve is using these local coordinates to describe the motion from the observer\'s <i>frame of reference</i>, that is, from a stationary point of view. In other words, although the local coordinate system moves with the particle, the observer does not. A change in coordinate system used by the observer is only a change in their <i>description</i> of observations, and does not mean that the observer has changed their state of motion, and <i>vice versa</i>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Ito-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Ito_23-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Zhilin Li; Kazufumi Ito (2006). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=_E084AX-iO8C&amp;pg=PA16&amp;dq=%22local+coordinates%22" rel="nofollow"><i>The immersed interface method: numerical solutions of PDEs involving interfaces and irregular domains</i></a>.
